< review>
Driving down the 101, on a whim we decided to check out the lake.  When we got to the toll booth we we're having second thoughts but it was half price to go in.  We went in after all and do not regret it one bit. Did the 4 mile rock trail hike which got us some amazing views of the lake as the clouds we're clearing out with sun shining all over.  What a beautiful place, make sure to check it out if you're a nature buff.</review>

< text>
Born and raised in Pittsburgh in the 50's, I was raised on "Jumbo" ( Pittsburghese term for bologna) on "chipped ham" (lower grade ham originally sold in Isaly's stores and chipped to very thin pieces who also sold the Klondike bar) and finally Swanson TV dinners. Swanson dinners were a mainstay back then & Carl Swanson from Sweden before moving to Omaha, had a revolutionary frozen food item. Too young to drink any wine and the "Burgh" was only known for Irom City Beer, I could never have imagined my roots would take me to running frozen food companies, exploring wineries in many countries as a hobby and recently just taking it all in at Swanson Vineyards. Amazing the full circle we can go on this wonderful journey called LIFE.

You probably already know most of the history about Swanson since W. Clarke Swanson, Jr. purchased the 100 acre property on Oak Knoll Rd. in 1985. What he & the rest of the family has done since then that makes them true trailblazers and visionaries for the crafting of the wines, the Interaction with the guests, grape varieties used and ingenious ways that they market, perfext planning, so here goes my brief tour from Vino Geno's perspective.

When I arrived by myself for my scheduled appointment I was met by my Salonnier, Sarah Dennis, yes a Salonnier who is the Keeper of the Salon. Very cool.

I just relaxed a bit outside in the very comfortable and shade filled area and had my first vino, a smooth '15 chard. That set the tone but wanted to move on from there. Swanson has focused on some core wines, most notably the trend setter merlot, the pinot grigio and the Alexis cab. Few know nor have enjoyed the bevy of other offerings here such a petit sirah, semillon, late harvest chard and a jacked up Petit Sirah.
Sarah was always available, gave me space and interacted when she felt I wanted to talk with her. Great Salonnier/ first one I ever met!
The property sits in the prized region of Napa with it's amazing DIRT. This property was among the first to design by appointment only but have taken it a few steps further with the other family members now contributing. The daughter, Alexis, launched the tasting salon and then the Sip Shoppe, almost 20 years ago. The Sip Shoppe is often referred to as the "CANDY store for adults". One gets the library vintages and a unique tasting menu. You have to check this out. Wines are poured in mini Riedel Os. Other gift ideas are there as well. If you are getting married the gift for you is there but I will not reveal it.

Sorry about the sidebar. But Swanson Winery has some incredible neighbors so it must be special. Not bad when your neighbors include Opus One, Caymus, Cakebread, Silver Oak, Plumpjack and Groth. Great company. Also phenomenal team members have worked at Swanson as well. It all started with a famous winemaker by the name of Andre Tchelistcheff and ramped up ever since with a tremendous list of winemakers over last 30+ years.

This brand knows how to market to their visitors and club members. Clarke focused on merlot and not cabernet sauvignon, and the complex and list of offerings is interesting. Easy to read up on all of these but just go and visit and snag a great Salonnier when you get there. It is easy to do but watch out guys as the women will want so many of the goodies they have there. But they are worth it. For me, I will savor the pour and the people I meet on this journey. I have a speccal list of Swanson wines, craft your own list, but I no longer crave Swnason TV dinners. Start with the bon vivant tasting & go from there with the chocolate later. OK, my choice is the Face Cabernet Vertical set of '08, '09 and '10, and throw in a bottle of 2012 Alexis cab, and while you are getting those also a 2013 merlot!< /text>

< text>
I enjoyed the course a lot. As a beginner, there were a few holes where I would accidentally swing my ball over onto another hole. The holes were fairly narrow, with a good amount of drive-able starts. Hole 13 can be fairly tricky, where there is a pond on the left and a park on the right. A very narrow margin to make it across safely. The fence was very shallow with no netting, so it was very dangerous for the cars on the other side. Overall, the course was challenging, but very fun!<//text>

<Text>This is the longest disc golf course in Orange County. Disc golfers are only allowed after 4pm. The course is lit in case you are out past sunset, but bring a flashlight with you just in case because the last 2 holes are poorly lit. $14 if you're walking and $19 if you want to play with a cart, which is recommended. On Mondays they have a PDGA sanctioned league for a few bucks more, and you don't need to be a PDGA member to register. They do dive for water discs periodically, and it's a small retrieval fee to get it back.<//Text><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMdE_qP3svIKB0XUip1cnnAo2eJD_dsOPbTAV04=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures><Response>None< /Response><Gmap_id>0x80dd279fe39785ed:0x88f92a6d5db8defe</Gmap_id></record>

<text>Pros:

Relatively long for an executive course so you get to bust out the driver (8 par 4's - 4 on each 9)

Lighted

Cheap (especially later in the day. After 4pm is like $18 to ride)

Cons:

Tee boxes, greens, and bunkers are usually not in the greatest shape (people don't seem to care about replacing divots, repairing ball marks, or raking the sand)

No cart service

No marshall (this can obviously be viewed as a pro as well depending on your habits)

Many lights are usually out (although many were recently replaced) and due to many leaves etc on the course it can be a challenge to find your ball at night)

Overall:

Great value! This is a really fun little (but longer than most executive courses) and challenging course that is easy on the wallet. Definitely recommend!< /text><pictures>None</pictures>< Response>

< Text>
Horrible Venue!!! If I could give negative stars I would. I had my wedding here on April 6th, 2018. Booking the venue was great initially. The events manager Chris Castro was super helpful, responded quickly and answered questions. A couple months after we booked he stopped responding and was impossible to get ahold of. Turns out he left the course to work elsewhere and was replaced by Nicole Lemus. Chris had promised my fianc√© comped rounds of golf for him and his groomsmen, golf carts to use around the facility the day of for pictures, the option to leave decorations overnight and pick up the next morning among other things. All were deciding factors for us when we booked. Nicole not only refused to make good on any of this, she was completely unorganized the day of the wedding and no idea what to do, what was happening or how a wedding is supposed to run. She was rude to my maid of honor and other guests. She did not request our guest count until a couple days before the event and then told us we were stuck paying for 120 people after I told her we only had 100 because it was "too late to change". She was nowhere to be found frequently during the evening. We were taking pictures on the course adjacent to the ceremony site and we were kicked off by staff because there were people still playing golf a couple holes away. All the lights in the reception room where turned completely on for most the beginning of the reception and during our first dance and not dimmed. She threw away our wedding cake and refused to give my MOH a box or container to take some home for me. Completely unprofessional and unacceptable! We are so disappointed in our choice of venue. This was supposed to be a special day and she made it more stressful and left us feeling so disappointed and upset. We spent about $10K to have our wedding here - and btw a 20% tip was automatically included - and I feel like we were completely ripped off. I know we will probably never get any money back but I hope this review helps others to NOT book this location for a wedding or any other event.</Text>

<Rate>3< /Rate><text>Not exactly what I was hoping for. Looking at the previous reviews, I was excited to try Shooters out. Sadly, it did not meet expectations. The games were not well organized, and there were too many players on the field at some times that did not create a competitive atmosphere, rather a run-n-duck game, because if you stuck your head out for more than three seconds, it was certain that 8 players had their barrels pointed at you. Some of the refs were friendly, others not so much. At some points I and my companions were treated more as 10 year old players rather than adults. The fields were okay quality, and it was hard to find shade. Though it wasn't a total plus, I would not recommend for veteran or non first time players. If the number of participants were split up to t pay on multiple fields, I think it would have created better game play. There are some positives though. < Review>
Not exactly what I was hoping for. Looking at the previous reviews, I was excited to try Shooters out. Sadly, it did not meet expectations. The games were not well organized, and there were too many players on the field at some times that did not create a competitive atmosphere, rather a run-n-duck game, because if you stuck your head out for more than three seconds, it was certain that 8 players had their barrels pointed at you. Some of the refs were friendly, others not so much. At some points I and my companions were treated more as 10 year old players rather than adults. The fields were okay quality, and it was hard to find shade. Though it wasn't a total plus, I would not recommend for veteran or non first time players. If the number of participants were split up to t pay on multiple fields, I think it would have created better game play. There are some positives though. The rental guns were in good condition and shot fairly accurately, and there is not much to complain about the paintballs (the masks, however, were as well as you would expect from renting). Overall, I had an ok experience, and most likely will not return. I wish Shooters the best of luck.</Review>

<user_id>102894549232968365253</user_id><text>My son and I went there last summer. We have been paint-ballers since for seven years and we have played on the fields in the Sacramento Area.
Problems with Shooters:
1. Check in is slow and crowded. One man was handling both check in and rentals. Before he got to us, he gave a safety briefing. The process lasted an hour, forty-five minutes longer than I have ever waited at other fields.
2. You have to keep masks on at the set-up tables. After a few games it grew tiresome.
3. You must use their paint. It did not matter that I brought a case of good paint from "Predator"; I had to dish out $50 extra.
4. The ref was bored and called the first game after 10 minutes.
5. Everyone except my son and I were rentals. By the third game we were so bored, we walked off.
6. They were having a 'scenario'. That meant there were unlimited responds, which was a nifty way for them to sell more paint.
Good points:

We were referred to Dr. Yazdi by our lactation consultant, Paula Santi, as a result of chronic breastfeeding issues (pain and recurring clogged ducts due to baby‚Äôs inefficient eating). Our LC recommended that we have a consultation for tight frenulum and consider frenectomy. We sought consultations with 2 doctors from Kaiser because we initially wanted to stay within our insurance network if we did decide to have the procedure. However, both Kaiser doctors seemed to know little about the mechanics of breastfeeding and convinced us that it was unlikely the procedure would have any effect on our breastfeeding experience. After the Kaiser consultations, we didn‚Äôt think we would have the procedure done. However, we didn‚Äôt want to give up hope of being able to breastfeed our son. So, when we shared the Kaiser experience with Paula, she suggested that we see Dr. Yazdi. I can‚Äôt even begin to say how happy I am that we took her advice. Dr. Yazdi was very knowledgeable on the subject as well as how ties impact the mechanics of breastfeeding. He took his time answer our extensive questions, and really listened to our concerns. We did not feel pressured at all to have the procedure. In response to others who say that he comes on strong, like he‚Äôs making a sales pitch, I would say, in our experience, he does have a ‚Äúpitch‚Äù but I think that he‚Äôs just trying to explain the mechanics of breastfeeding and how the anatomy of the baby‚Äôs mouth needs to work together to breastfeed effectively. This involves educating the patient, and my husband and I appreciated that educational piece of the consultation; perhaps others do not. Also, I‚Äôm not questioning others who say he pressured them to have the procedure...maybe he did. But, that was not our experience. He gave us the room to talk it over, and we decided to have the tongue and lip tie corrected that day. The procedure itself was incredibly fast. The baby came out with a little blood on his lip. We were told that is normal, and, indeed, the bleeding stopped right away, and he nursed immediately. The first feed I used a nipple shield so could not gauge if the pain associated with his latch diminished, but he seemed to be eating pretty efficiently. The second feed after the procedure I nursed without the use of the shield and that‚Äôs when I became a firm believer that this procedure can have amazing results. After months of struggling with blistered and bleeding nipples, my baby finally latched with no pain and had a full feed in 30 minutes. He was so milk drunk afterwards. It was amazing. He did become pretty fussy that night and we were assured that‚Äôs to be expected. Since the procedure yesterday we‚Äôve had multiple feeds without the use of the nipple shield, with no pain to me and a well fed, satisfied baby. I know that this doesn‚Äôt work for everyone and that results are not always so immediate, but for us it was incredible, and I‚Äôm so glad we decided to have it done by Dr. Yazdi and his wonderful team!</Text>

< Review>
Lack of humanity on management! My iphone and wallet was stolen from my car last evening. Good samaritan customers in the store were calling it and my apple watch indicated it was still in the store, and then suddenly my phone was turned off completely. Therefore, the thief was in the store. The security guard told me a man left the store in a hurry, who may or may not have been the thief. I asked management to call over the intercom to announce that if anyone found the phone to please turn it in to the front, still giving the benefit of the doubt to thief and to give an opportunity to return. Management refused and said it was a liability to announce that a phone/wallet was "lost." I think the true liability was that my phone was stolen in the store, with a security guard standing present. They said that if they called for my lost wallet and phone, then they would be doing that all day. It was in these few minutes they could have acted to have potentially made a difference. Now we will never know. Management advised that I call the police. I asked the security guard the description of the man who left the store in a hurry. They wouldn't give me a description. I understand that the man may not have been the thief, but to withhold that information is truly too cautionary. Either way, the thief has no access to my phone since it is attached to my account and I canceled my cards before they had opportunity to use it. However, it's a true disappointment that management did nothing to assist a patron, who was a victim of theft directly in their store, and on the day before Thanksgiving no less. They need to gain some wisdom. Their fear of liability outweighed their humanity. The true liability is that they did nothing to assist in mitigating the opportunity for the thief to leave the store, by acting in good faith and making a simple announcement over the intercom. If a thief knew that the whole store was looking for that phone, that potentially could have made a difference.< /Review>
